<div id="review_641546538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641546538" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3739451-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352731541p2/3739451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641546538?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/3739451-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312429027" href="/book/show/6621383-dancer">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Suzanne by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/632247-chrissie">Chrissie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=geocaching-challenge-2016">geocaching-challenge-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=2017-survey-says-annual-challenge">2017-survey-says-annual-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=dance">dance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641546538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3312706913496063130"><i>Dancer</i> is a work of fiction about the life of Rudolf Nureyev. I am a balletomane. I first became enchanted with the art form when I read a book about Vaslav Nijinski in high school. Then my aunt took me to see the Royal Danish Ballet perform Coppelia at NYC's Metropolitan Opera House. I was hooked. While I never got to see Nureyev dance, SHE did. And seeing Nureyev with Margot Fonteyn was the catalyst that ignited HER interest in ballet. Today my son is training to be a professional ballet dance</span>
  <span id="freeText3312706913496063130" style="display:none"><i>Dancer</i> is a work of fiction about the life of Rudolf Nureyev. I am a balletomane. I first became enchanted with the art form when I read a book about Vaslav Nijinski in high school. Then my aunt took me to see the Royal Danish Ballet perform Coppelia at NYC's Metropolitan Opera House. I was hooked. While I never got to see Nureyev dance, SHE did. And seeing Nureyev with Margot Fonteyn was the catalyst that ignited HER interest in ballet. Today my son is training to be a professional ballet dancer, and I have a special interest in male danseurs.<br /><br />Going from Nijinski to Nureyev, you see an obvious connection. It's not about their nationality, however, it's their state of mind. They were both men obsessed with their art. It drove Nijinski to madness. I believe Nureyev suffered from another form of mental disability. Dance became so much a part of him, that he did not relate well to others. He seemed to lack empathy. His best friends, Erik Bruhn (who was his lover) and Margot Fonteyn, did indeed love him, but it perhaps it was because they understood and respected his passion for dance.<br /><br />McCann captured Nureyev quite well. There was a real sense of his dance-focus, and his self-centered personality. The author also expertly lays the backdrop of Soviet Russia, along with the staggering fame, paranoia and hard-hitting party life that led Rudi down a perverse path that would eventually kill him. My only complaint was the way the McCann changed narrators - often and in a confusing way. There were many times it took me pages to figure out who was telling the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3312706913496063130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_55861651" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55861651" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/617334-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275908303p2/617334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55861651?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/617334-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805067927" href="/book/show/1409133.Dancer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=socialism">socialism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=dance">dance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=russia">russia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55861651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10229089759138295432">1. I know only a little about Nureyev (if you want, you can watch him <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zQVoBaw1AGU' rel='nofollow noopener'>on The Muppet Show</a>, among other things), but while I think more knowledge would have enriched parts of <i>Dancer</i>, I am glad that I didn't know too much. It's an odd kind of historical fiction, not quite a biographical novel, but like one: the differences between fact and fiction are blurry. I really liked that experience, and I think it made the book richer.<br/><br/>2. McCann mixes first and third person narrative passages very effectivel</span>
  <span id="freeText10229089759138295432" style="display:none">1. I know only a little about Nureyev (if you want, you can watch him <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zQVoBaw1AGU" rel="nofollow noopener">on The Muppet Show</a>, among other things), but while I think more knowledge would have enriched parts of <i>Dancer</i>, I am glad that I didn't know too much. It's an odd kind of historical fiction, not quite a biographical novel, but like one: the differences between fact and fiction are blurry. I really liked that experience, and I think it made the book richer.<br /><br />2. McCann mixes first and third person narrative passages very effectively, bordering them with information from the historical record (although - as you can tell from the opening page which lists things thrown onstage during Nureyev's first Paris season - dance happily crosses the line between legend and history). The first person passages are from people peripheral to Nureyev's story (I suppose some of them of them are complete fabrications) - they are all very interesting characters. And they arouse sympathy, although they are less difficult people than Nureyev, so that reaction isn't really much of a surprise. I liked the kaleidoscope effect very much - it really enriched the story. Although I think a more straightforward historical novel would also have been interesting (and containing its own challenges).<br /><br />3. The first book, with the descriptions of Russia during World War II, is worth a look for itself alone. There is a magnificent and devastating power there. Whether or not you give a damn about dance!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10229089759138295432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874704696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874704696" />
    <a title="Christine Boyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2538232-christine-boyer"><img alt="Christine Boyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379634098p2/2538232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874704696?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Boyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Boyer" href="/user/show/2538232-christine-boyer">Christine Boyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312429027" href="/book/show/6621383-dancer">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Men and women who enjoy life's dramas</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874704696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2242514743802682746">Really more like 4.5 stars. I'm a new fan of Colum McCann! The writing was incredible! Strong imagery, poetic, and many memorable lines and moments.<br/><br/>This is NOT a biography. In fact, it says right on the front "novel". It is fiction. In fact, in an interesting way, it is not even about Nureyev's dancing, even though that might be the expectation of some readers since that's how we all knew him. I, for one, was glad it wasn't a chronicle of his many, many ballet performances - snooze. <br/><br/>Instead, it </span>
  <span id="freeText2242514743802682746" style="display:none">Really more like 4.5 stars. I'm a new fan of Colum McCann! The writing was incredible! Strong imagery, poetic, and many memorable lines and moments.<br /><br />This is NOT a biography. In fact, it says right on the front "novel". It is fiction. In fact, in an interesting way, it is not even about Nureyev's dancing, even though that might be the expectation of some readers since that's how we all knew him. I, for one, was glad it wasn't a chronicle of his many, many ballet performances - snooze. <br /><br />Instead, it is more of an insight on how we each choose to live our lives and whether we're happy with our choices or regretful about them. <br /><br />Just some items to be aware of: During the middle of the book there are long, detailed sections describing explicit gay sexual encounters. Also, McCann uses different grammatical &amp; literary techniques, i.e., no quotation marks, a run-on sentence which went for 36 pages without a period, frequent point-of-view switches, random thoughts. The story was so fascinating and the writing was so solid that I wasn't bothered by the sex or variations of writing, but it's something you should know before diving in! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2242514743802682746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Joanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/940357-joanna"><img alt="Joanna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3441305150?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna" href="/user/show/940357-joanna">Joanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3441305150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7174017905466703167">It was just out of stubbornness that I pushed through to finish this book, and I guess a desire to find out how it/Nureyev's life ended. I thought it would be interesting to learn more about Nureyev, his history, and life in the USSR during his lifetime, but I don't feel I got a good sense of either. Each chapter is told from a different perspective which, instead of providing insight through different sets of eyes, was confusing. None of the characters was developed enough (including Nureyev) t</span>
  <span id="freeText7174017905466703167" style="display:none">It was just out of stubbornness that I pushed through to finish this book, and I guess a desire to find out how it/Nureyev's life ended. I thought it would be interesting to learn more about Nureyev, his history, and life in the USSR during his lifetime, but I don't feel I got a good sense of either. Each chapter is told from a different perspective which, instead of providing insight through different sets of eyes, was confusing. None of the characters was developed enough (including Nureyev) to have any depth or provide the reader with any understanding of their lives and actions. Nureyev comes across as completely unlikable and worse at times. The best part was the very beginning when he was a child and you do feel you get a small sense of growing up in communist Russia, and as a boy who doesn't fit the mold of his male peers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7174017905466703167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_15965076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15965076" />
    <a title="Gretchen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/180929-gretchen"><img alt="Gretchen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434059181p2/180929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15965076?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gretchen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gretchen" href="/user/show/180929-gretchen">Gretchen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180929-gretchen?shelf=soultouching">soultouching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180929-gretchen?shelf=barnes-and-noble-bargain-buys">barnes-and-noble-bargain-buys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15965076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15815805494334262722">Beautiful!!! That is the word which best describes this biographical novel of Rudi Nureyev the great Russian ballet dancer who began life as a boy in communist Russia to later defect and live a glamorous life of opulence around the world. Rudi's story is told from the point of view of those nearest and dearest to him and while at times he seems almost completely unsympathetic based on his compulsive and diva like behaviors, the author strives to find his most human qualities and paints a beautif</span>
  <span id="freeText15815805494334262722" style="display:none">Beautiful!!! That is the word which best describes this biographical novel of Rudi Nureyev the great Russian ballet dancer who began life as a boy in communist Russia to later defect and live a glamorous life of opulence around the world. Rudi's story is told from the point of view of those nearest and dearest to him and while at times he seems almost completely unsympathetic based on his compulsive and diva like behaviors, the author strives to find his most human qualities and paints a beautiful picture of a haunted man. Though the book never explicitly states the cause of Rudi's death, it is painfully obvious based on his promiscuous lifestyle and the descriptions of his declining health that he was among those felled by AIDS before the disease became known as it is today. Reading this book, I wanted to find a tape so that I could see the dancer in all of his glory as he had been described so brilliantly upon the page. This is by far one of my best buys off of the Barnes and Noble Bargain shelf to date.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15815805494334262722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hQBB8IpyFPLJpe+p3Qw5GZyRWspwOv4qZ40ZXEZ8ulU11NO2/u7eb1eNVMVYVjKt/BvUcp+u0yY2cgk0D7Vvvw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TfPBdjQPFGBb5asfJIfga2YXl7fA7Btom/KqA2NhCrz9J1MwQJPe/cXNEHOh3evfBp0ZDy94NmTKDbprKqjfVg==')})
  }

In Out of the Mountains, David Kilcullen, one of t<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3630555611462476588\" style=\"display:none\">When Americans think of modern warfare, what comes to mind is the US army skirmishing with terrorists and insurgents in the mountains of Afghanistan. But the face of global conflict is ever-changing. In Out of the Mountains, David Kilcullen, one of the world\'s leading experts on current and future conflict, offers a groundbreaking look at what may happen after today\'s wars end. This is a book about future conflicts and future cities, and about the challenges and opportunities that four powerful megatrends-- population, urbanization, coastal settlement, and connectedness-- are creating across the planet. And it is about what cities, communities and businesses can do to prepare for a future in which all aspects of human society--including, but not limited to, conflict, crime and violence--are changing at an unprecedented pace. Kilcullen argues that conflict is increasingly likely to occur in sprawling coastal cities, in peri-urban slum settlements that are enveloping many regions of the Middle East, Africa, Latin America and Asia, and in highly connected, electronically networked settings. He suggests that cities, rather than countries, are the critical unit of analysis for future conflict and that resiliency, not stability, will be the key objective. Ranging across the globe--from Kingston to Mogadishu to Lagos to Benghazi to Mumbai-- he offers a unified theory of &quot;competitive control&quot; that explains how non-state armed groups such as drug cartels, street gangs, and warlords draw their strength from local populations, providing useful ideas for dealing with these groups and with diffuse social conflicts in general. His extensive fieldwork on the ground in a series of urban conflicts suggests that there will be no military solution for many of the struggles we will face in the future. Based on years of persistent detective work, Last Ditch investigates the German plans and the countermeasures undertaken through the specially formed British Resistance Organization. The very existence of this Resistance movement remained a secret for more than two decades until the silence was finally broken by Lampe. Few would have escaped oppression. There was to be mass deportation, wholesale appropriations of the country’s agricultural, mineral, and industrial produce, and widespread arrests, as revealed in the notorious Gestapo Arrest List-reprinted here in full. Although they never went into action, the Resistance was ready and waiting: the last ditch of Britain’s defense. So successful was their organization that they became the model for the Resistance and underground movements that were to arise all over occupied Europe. Indeed, his vision of modern<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17634729190926847687\" style=\"display:none\">David Kilcullen is one of the world\'s most influential experts on counterinsurgency and modern warfare, a ground-breaking theorist whose ideas &quot;are revolutionizing military thinking throughout the west&quot; (Washington Post). Indeed, his vision of modern warfare powerfully influenced America\'s decision to rethink its military strategy in Iraq and implement &quot;the Surge,&quot; now recognized as a dramatic success.  In The Accidental Guerrilla, Kilcullen provides a remarkably fresh perspective on the War on Terror. Kilcullen takes us &quot;on the ground&quot; to uncover the face of modern warfare, illuminating both the big global war (the &quot;War on Terrorism&quot;) and its relation to the associated &quot;small wars&quot; across the globe: Iraq, Afghanistan, Indonesia, Thailand, the Pakistani tribal zones, East Timor and the horn of Africa. Kilcullen sees today\'s conflicts as a complex interweaving of contrasting trends--local insurgencies seeking autonomy caught up in a broader pan-Islamic campaign--small wars in the midst of a big one. He warns that America\'s actions in the war on terrorism have tended to conflate these trends, blurring the distinction between local and global struggles and thus enormously complicating our challenges. Indeed, the US had done a poor job of applying different tactics to these very different situations, continually misidentifying insurgents with limited aims and legitimate grievances--whom he calls &quot;accidental guerrillas&quot;--as part of a coordinated worldwide terror network. We must learn how to disentangle these strands, develop strategies that deal with global threats, avoid local conflicts where possible, and win them where necessary. Colored with gripping battlefield experiences that range from the jungles and highlands of Southeast Asia to the mountains of the Afghanistan-Pakistan border to the dusty towns of the Middle East, The Accidental Guerrilla will, quite simply, change the way we think about war.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/14080.Colum_McCann">About Colum McCann</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/14080.Colum_McCann"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1566733372p3/14080.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/14080.Colum_McCann">Colum McCann
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,989
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4887611125646432109">Sign up for Colum's newsletter: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bit.ly/mccannsignup'>http://bit.ly/mccannsignup</a><br/><br/>Colum McCann is the author of three collections of short stories and six novels, including "Apeirogon," due to be published in Spring 2020. His other books include "TransAtlantic," "Let the Great World Spin," "This Side of Brightness,""Dancer" and “Zoli,” all of which were international best-sellers. <br/><br/>“Let the Great World Spin” won the Natio</span>
  <span id="freeText4887611125646432109" style="display:none">Sign up for Colum's newsletter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/mccannsignup">http://bit.ly/mccannsignup</a><br /><br />Colum McCann is the author of three collections of short stories and six novels, including "Apeirogon," due to be published in Spring 2020. His other books include "TransAtlantic," "Let the Great World Spin," "This Side of Brightness,""Dancer" and “Zoli,” all of which were international best-sellers. <br /><br />“Let the Great World Spin” won the National Book Award in 2009. His fiction has been published in over 40 languages and has appeared in The New Yorker, The Atlantic Monthly, GQ, Paris Review and other places. He has written for numerous publications including The Irish Times, Die Zeit, La Republicca, Paris Match, The New York Times, the Guardian and the Independent. <br /><br />Colum has won numerous international awards and has been a bestseller on four continents. He is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters, as well as the Irish association of artists, Aosdana. He has also received a Chevalier des Artes et des Lettres from the French government. He is the cofounder of the global non-profit story exchange organisation Narrative 4. <br /><br />In 2003 Colum was named Esquire magazine's "Writer of the Year." Other awards and honors include a Pushcart Prize, the Rooney Prize, the Irish Independent Hughes and Hughes/Sunday Independent Novel of the Year 2003, and the 2002 Ireland Fund of Monaco Princess Grace Memorial Literary Award. He was recently inducted into the Hennessy Hall of Fame for Irish Literature. <br /><br />His short film "Everything in this Country Must," directed by Gary McKendry, was nominated for an Academy Award Oscar in 2005. <br /><br />Colum was born in Dublin in 1965 and began his career as a journalist in The Irish Press. In the early 1980's he took a bicycle across North America and then worked as a wilderness guide in a program for juvenile delinquents in Texas. After a year and a half in Japan, he and his wife Allison moved to New York where they currently live with their three children, Isabella, John Michael and Christian. <br /><br />Colum teaches in Hunter College in New York, in the Creative Writing program, with fellow novelists Peter Carey and Tea Obreht. <br /><br />Colum has completed his new novel, "Apeirogon." Crafted out of a universe of fictional and nonfictional material, McCann tells the story of Bassam Aramin and Rami Elhanan. One is Israeli. One is Palestinian. Both are fathers. Both have lost their daughters to the conflict. When Bassam and Rami learn of each other's stories they recognize the loss that connects them, and they begin to use their grief as a weapon for peace. <br /><br />In the novel McCann crosses centuries and continents. He stitches together time, art, history, nature and politics in a tale both heartbreaking and hopeful. Musical, cinematic, muscular, delicate and soaring, Apeirogon is a novel for our times.<br /><br />It is scheduled for release in the U.S in February 2020. <br /> <br /><br />Advance copies will be available here on GoodReads!!!! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4887611125646432109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
